CHINA
LIAONING URBAN INFRASTRUCTURE PROJECT
CREDIT AND PROJECT SUMMARY
Borrower:          People's Republic of Chinra.
Bencficiaries:    Liaoning Province and the Municipalitie-. of Shenyarig, Fuxin
and Yingkou.
Credit Amount:    SDR 54.2 million (US$77.8 million equivalent).
Terms:             Standard, with 35 years maturity.
Onlending          From the Government of China to Liaoning Province for 15
Terms:             years, including five years of grace, at a fixed interest
rate of 5.5 percent per annum; from Liaoning Province to the
Municipalities on the same terms. Foreign exchange risks
will be borne by the Municipalities.
From the Municipalities to the Water Supply Companies: 15
years, including 5 years of grace, at the variable interest
rate payable on medium/long-term Renminbi loans by the
People's Construction Bank of China.
Project            The project has the broad objectives of improving the
Description:       utilization and management of water resources and urban
transport services in Liaoning Province, an important
industrial base in China. The project would assist in the
initial phase of an investment program aimed at addressing
the shortages and poor quality of water supply in the cities
of Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou, and shortcomings in urban
transport in Shenyang. The specific objectives of the
project are: (a) to improve water supply conditions in the
three project cities through physical works and
strengthening of institutions, regulations, management,
financial and pricing policies; (b) to improve traffic and
public transport conditions in Shenyang through a pilot
program of selected low-cost physical work,s and
institutional strengthening; and (c) to improve measures for
water pollution abatement through technical assistance in
wastewater treatment, and strengthening of institutions and
enforcement measures for water pollution control.
The water supplv component in Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou
would develop physical works, including transmission and
distribution pipelines, water intake works, pumping
stations, and water treatment works, as well as provide
training and technical assistance for the local water
companies, the Liaoning Construction Commission, the Urban



- vi -
companies, the Liaoning Construction Commission, the Urban
and Rural Construction Commissions of the three
municipalities and the Liaoning Water Resource Commission.
The component would include, iter alia, a study of water
resource and water supply pricing. A water pollution
control component would provide technical assistance for a
study of industrial wastewater treatment arnd environmental
regulations. In addition, equipment would he acquired for
environmental monitoring. The urban transport component,
which would be concentrated in Shenyang, would impro';e about
+4 km of arterial road corridors, and provide equipment,
technical assistance and training to support management of
public transport operations, in particular, road and public
vehicle maintenance, road safety measures and operations
management. To facilitate project planning and management,
training would be provided to staff of the project offices,
the Liaoning Construction Commission and the water supply
and public transport companies. Technical assistance would
be included in the project to assist the Provincial
Government in planning and design of a second phase of the
investment program, which would focus on water pollution
abatement.
Benefits:          The improved water supply would provide much needed drinking
water to the population, as well as inputs for industrial
development in the three cities. Benefits from the water
components would also come from improved health conditions
of the city residents, particularly those residing in lower
income areas, through better water availability and reduced
ingress of contaminated groundwater into the water mains.
The urban transport component would relieve traffic
congestion in central city areas of Slienyang. Benefits
would accrue from personal savings associated with shorter
travel times, savings in vehicle operating costs and
reduction in traffic accidents. Other important benefits of
this project include improvements in project planning and
management, and introduction of better financial discipline
for the water supply companies.
Risks:             Possible project risks include insufficient commitment of
the Liaoning Government and the three Municipal Governments
to pursue the significant pricing policy reforms and
institutional changes required, to provide the necessary
counterpart funds for implementing the project, and to raise
the necessary funds to fully implement the proposed
development program. The project has built-in measures to
minimize these risks. These include technical assistance to
study tariffs and tariff structures required to meet
economic and financial objectives, assurance from Liaoning
Government for the timely provision of counterpart funds,
and the building up of an effective planning institution to
follow up on the implementation of the development program.

CHiiNA
LIAONINC URBAN INFRASTRUCTURE PROJECT
I. THE URBAN. WATER SUPPLY AND TRANSPORT SECTORS
Utb;it-tization in China
1.1       During the 1960s and 1970s, China's cities grew moderately, in
terms of population, economic activity, incomes, urban infrastructure, housiing
stock and services. Since 1979, however, the urban sector has experienced a
dynamism unprecedented since 1950. With the re-introduction of household
tarms, the liberalization of agricultural pricing, and the spread of
igricultural markets free from government price ceilings, China entered a
period of rapid economic growth and rising incomes. In the cities,
administrative restrictions on tile expansion of light industries and service
activities were lifted, while the growth of household incomes fueled an
untprecedented surge in demand for urban goods and services.
1.2       As a result of this expansion, urban managers are being confronted
with a growing demand for urban public services and its associated
infrastructure, from both enterprises and households. No longer is there any
doubt that a strong link exists be.ween the development of the local economic
base and the expansion of the area's infrastructure. The legitimacy of
household demand for improved public services and better housing is also
accepted. Population growth rates have begun to approach levels not
experienced since the 1950s, as the demand for labor encourages a relaxation
of migration controls. Cities that had stagnated for two decades now find
themselves with built-up areal populations expanding at a rate of 4 percent
to 5 percent per year. This phenomenon has helped prompt the central
government to reconsider its approach to planning, financing, and managing
urban development. Recent statistics are, however, showing a decline in the
urban built-up population growth rate in large cities, which is expected to
stabilize to around 1 percent by the year 2000.
1.3       The central government's modernization-through-reform movement has
included new features such as an increased emphasis on foreign trade, greater
itnvolvement by foreign investors, directives for state-owned economic
enterprises to concentrate on profit-maximizing behavior, the renewal of
private economic activity, and the liberalization of labor markets. As a
result, local governments and their public utility companies have begun to
accept the fact that, increasingly, cities must compete with one another to
attract new economic activity and encourage existing enterprises to expand as
efficiently as possible. The challenge facing China's cities is how best to
match the requirements created by rapid and sustained economic growth with a
program of urban development investments and accompanying management, fiscal
and policy measures. The central government is now limiting itself largely to
encouraging the process of restructuring urban development by setting broad
objectives and parameters.
This is the area of densest development, which is provided with a full
complement of urban services.



':It   Itji    I y
China h<a; an average potential water reserve of about 2,800 billion
p,i vt';r, or an annual per capita average water reserve of about 2,400 in3
i14 thB 1a jor u';er ot water inl China is agriculture, water needs itl urbani
alre rapidly' rising.  By the end of 1988 about 34 million m3 per day of
I   Lter were used by roughly 170 milliont urban dwellers (about 84 percent
(ft t II I rban populat ioll covered by piped supply), and another 64 million in3
per daty for industries in tthe cities, giving a total of 98 million m3 per day
Or alboLlt f36 billion ml per year. Tentative projections by the cities show
watc1 nteeds to grow to 85 billion m3 per year by the year 2000.  Industries
u;e over 60 percent of the city water supply, with little attention given to
onservaLtionl of water.2 Serious water shortages are found in many cities.
iow,-ver, inost cities lack the financial resources for the relatively large
investments required for water source development, and expansion of water
treatment and distribution facilities to meet additional water needs. Faced
with this reality, many cities are now moving toward stringent demand
management measures.
1.5       Associated with water supply is the related problem of water
pollution. Industries are without dispute the worst polluters. Most
factories are not equipped for pollution control, and effluents containing
high concentrations of toxic matter, heavy metals and organic materials are
discharged into the environment with little or no treatment. While water
pollution control regulations exist, most polluting industries have thus far
been delinquent on the implementation of pollution abatement measures on the
grounds of technical and financial difficulties. There is, however, rapidly
growing awareness about environmental degradation and its serious impact on
living conditions, in particular the effect of pollution on the quality of
water resources needed for the country's economic development. Already many
cities are tightening enforcement of industrial effluent standards. The law
for a country-wide pollution permit system has been passed requiring
registration of enterprises that pollute. These permits may be revoked if
effective pollution abatement measures are not taken. Implementation of these
measures is expected to be gradual, given the time needed for industries to
plan and carry out the large investments required.
1.6       Urban wastewater in China is normally collected through separate
sanitary sewers or combined sewers (the latter carrying both wastewater and
rainwater). Sewage treatment facilities are absent or grossly inadequate in
most cities. While sewerage charges are allowed by the Central Authorities,
as yet not many cities have adopted these principles, and those that charge
have not been doing it in the most efficient way. While the city water supply
is usually run on a utility basis in China, most cities have municipal
departments that operate the sewerage system on the city budget. That a
utility form of organization for sewerage can bring about better management is
being accepted in China, and many cities are already exploring suitable
organizational changes .3
2    Chinese industries consume about 3 to 10 times the water for similar
industries in many industrialized countries.

Urban Transport
1.8       Urbar. transport problems in all major Chinese cities are sev      ,!
worseninlg.  In the larger cities, transit times are excessive througholt( ti,.
day on most main corridors leading to the central business diEtrict (CI3D) a,,d
to large industrial areas. These problems stem from: (a) inadequate road
space -- roads occupy about 7 percent of the total urban area of cities in
China, compared to 20-25 percent in developed countries; (b) poor utilizati(I:
of the road space due to the intermixing of motorized and non-motorized
vehicles; (c) poor road discipline and safety enforcement; and (d) severe
underinvestment in the public transport systems.
1.9       In urban China, the number of persons per motorized vehicle 1an?ge,-
from 30-85 persons per vehicle, which is very lcw. On the other hand, the
number of persons per bicycle ranges from 1.2 to 2.1. With virtually rio
increase in bus fares for about twenty years and difficulties in obtaining
municipal funds, investment in the bus and trolley systems has been low.
Large numbers of public transport vehicles, which have long passed their
useful life and are prone to frequent mechanical breakdowns, are still on the
roads. In Shenyang, as in many other cities, the situation has deteriorated
to such a point, that it is faster to ride a bicycle (travelling at an average
speea of 10.9 km/hr) in the CBD and other congested areas than to use public
transport (7.2 km/hr). The number of private cars in China is very low --
about 170 to 320 persons per vehicle, and the number of motorcycles has been
restricted in most cities.
1.10      The immediate need is to address the current conflict in use of
road space between motorized and non-motorized vehicles. This is proposed to
be achieved by (a) increasing the availability of road space through road
widening, providing vehicle separation barriers, resurfacing and redesign of
road intersections; (b) increasing efficiency of road use through better
traffic regulation, enforcement and management; and (c) improving the
operation and availability of public transport.
Sector Organization
1.11      The Ministry of Water Conservancy is the central organization
responsible for determining policies on the allocation and management of
surface water resources in the country. The implementation of these policies
is carried out through river basin commissions, provincial water conservancy
departments and water conservancy bureaus at various local government levels.
Allocation and management of groundwater is, however, the responsibility of
the Ministry of Geology and Minerals and the corresponding local government
departments and bureaus. The National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA),
separated in 1988 from the Ministry of Urban and Rural Construction and
Environmental Protection (MURCEP), is responsible for setting environmental
policies and providing guidance to the provinces on environmental matters.
1.12      The Ministry of Communications (MOCOM) is responsible for national
transport policies and investment strategies (inter-modal and inter-regional).

1.13      Each province and cenitrally-controlled municipality is responsiblhe
for urban infrastructure works in its cities and towns and for (ntivirotimelittal
protection under its jurisdiction, executed through various proVin(iatl
commissions and departments. Overseeing urban matters are tihe provincial
commissions of planning and construction, and the department of finance, wlich
approve urban plans and major projects for cities and towns.  The actual work
of planning and design of projects is carried out by municipal bureaus arid,
for large projects, provincial guidance and assistance would be sought. In
the past construction work was normally carried out by construction units
within the host municipal bureaus. Increasingly it is being contracted out
through a competitive bidding process to construction enterprises, most of
which have been reorganized from the original construction units, that now
compete for work outside of their own complex. All large urban projects are
reported to MOC. Large projects (exceeding Y 200 million) require approval by
the State Planning Commission (SPC). Those involving foreign loans require
approval by both the SPC and the State Council.
Sectoral Issues
1.14      For at least two decades prior to the 1980s, China had concentrated
on industrialization in urban areas, but had left urban services seriously
neglected. Although in the past decade China's cities and towns have invested
considerable resources to improve urban infrastructure, the urban sector will
need to continue large scale investments for the foreseeable future in order
to sustain economic growth and environmental quality. Careful investment
planning with prudent selection of investment priorities are therefore
critical issues. Increasingly urban investments would need to he funded from
local resources, and, therefore, upgrading of local government financing is
another area of concern.
1.15      While there is recognition at the various levels of government of
excessive water use by industry, measures to convert manufacturing processes
to conserve water are often costly. Unless industries are given appropriate
incentives, excessive water use cannot be abated. To address the situation,
Chinese cities are currently setting water use quotas for various industries
with heavy financial penalties for exceeding the quotas. This, in effect, is
a form of two tier charging system. The rules for quota levels are, however,
arbitrarily defined, and the penalties charged do not reflect resource cost.
Formalization of a policy to tie these charges with the marg.nal cost of water
production and distribution will be needed, in order to ensure that water is
used economically. Realistic consumption levels on this basis could then be
obtained to provide a more reasonable base for cities to plan their water
supplies.

1.17      NEPA and the provincial and municipal environmental protection
bureaus hlave set guidelines and regulations to govern wastewater discharges.
hIowever, these agencies do not have sufficient power to deal with large
inidustries (the major polluters), which usually have very strong political
support.  Consequently, measures to abate pollution, such as the levying of
pollution charges, have often not been effective, as the chatges have
frequently been forcibly depressed so that polluting industries would rather
pay pollution charges than take appropriate measures to reduce pollution.
Most provincial governments are already aware of the need for environmental
protection, and some measures are already being taken (para. 1.5).
Strengthening and equipping environmental protection bureaus and training of
their staffs to carry out pollution control functions effectively would be
urgently needed.
1.18      The traffic situation in cities has been deteriorating over the
past few years as indicated by decreasing travel speeds in the CBD and an
increasing number of accidents. With heavy competition for limited city
development funds for capital works, urban transport projects need to
emphasize low-cost improvement and operational efficiency. The thrust for
such improvements would lie in improving the utilization of the current road
system and upgrading the public transport system to make it a more desireable
mode of travel. There is a need to introduce improved concepts and design of
urban transport and road systems. Local officials in charge of urban
transport need to be trained in design, operation, management, and traffic
regulations enforcement. For the public transport system, operations need to
be made more efficient through better route and schedule design, and improved
maintenance of public transport vehicles.
Previous Operations and Sector Work
1.19      The Bank Group is involved in three projects in China's urban and
water supply sectors, which are now under implementation. These are:
(a)  The China Rural Water Supply Project (Credit 1578-CHA, SDR 82.1
million, 1985) to finance equipment, goods, civil works, training,
and devalopment of management and monitoring systems for water
supply systems in about 4,650 villages, of four provinces and
Beijing Municipality. Water supply to about 75 percent of the
project villages has now been completed. Project completion is
scheduled for 1991.
(b)  The Shanghai Sewerage Project (Credit 1779-CHA, SDR 78.9 million,
1987; Loan 2794-CHA, US$45 million, 1987) to finance a link and
intercepting sewer system to collect, transport and treat
wastewater for disposal in the estuary of the Changjiang; studies
on management and organization, sewerage tariff, Huangpu River



- 6 -
l,sjnt management, and sewer system rehabilitation; ani( statf
training. Project implementation is on schedule with project
completion expected by December 1992.
,)  Thie Medium Cities Planning and Management Project (Credit 21001-CHA,
SOR 62.2 million, Loan 3286-CHA, US$79.4 million, 1991) to finarice
investmenits in education and health services, housing,
transportation, water supply and sewerage, industrial development
and pollution control in three medium sized cities, Changzhou,
Shashi and Luoyang.  Included also is technical assistance for
urban planning and management. Project implementation commenced in
January 1991 and is scheduled for completion in December 1996.
1.20      Sector work carried out by the Bank Group includes: (a) the
Sh,inglhai Sector Memorandum (Urban), Report No. 4227-CHA, December 1982; (b) a
Bank Group economic report, China -- Long-term Development Issues and Options,
Report No. 5206- CHA, May 22, 1985, which includes a chapter on spatial and
urban issues; (c) an urban sector survey in Liaoning province in 1985 in
cooperation with UNDP and AIDAB; and (d) an urban sector study in Zhejiang
Province, China --Zheiiang: Challenges of Rapid Urbanization, Report No. 6612-
CHA, August 3, 1987. Currently under preparation are a "Housing Reform Sector
Study", focusing on options for housing reform in China, and an "Environmental
Strategy Study" to help formulate long-term environmental protection and
natural resource policies and programs.
Bank Group's Role and Sector Lending Strategy
1.21      The Bank Group sees its principal role as fostering a continuing
dialogue on sector issues and options, thereby helping to map the transition
to urban development planning that is decentralized, more market-responsive,
efficient, and sensitive to equity and the need for environmental protection.
The Bank Group's approach is to: (a) invest resources in understanding issues
and options through sector studies; (b) provide the central authorities with
analyses in areas requiring central government action; and (c) build or,
project experience elsewhere and, through the financing of infrastructure and
technical assistance, help improve overall local planning and the planning and
management of those sectors that are primarily the responsibility of local
authorities. The spatial priorities of the program reflect those of the
central government: first, to target the large urban centers most closely
linked to the opening to the outside world; second, to become involved in
multi-city coastal provincial projects; and third, to work selectively with
cities of moderate size.
1.22      The Bank Group has developed a sector strategy which addresses the
key sector issues. Analytical work and lending operations are aimed toward
assisting China's central and local governments to: (a) introduce tools that
define local spatial and investment priorities; (b) utilize existing
facilities more effectively through non-construction measures; (c) enable
sector managers at the local level to adopt planning and management tools that
are more demand-responsive and utilize project selection criteria that
incorporate economlc and financial as well as technical perspectives; (d)
encourage greater cost recovery from users of public utilities' services; and
(e) operationalize environmental resource management in urban areas through
establishment of appropriate institutional and financing mechanisms.



II.  PROJECIT BACKGROUND
Project Background
2.1        In 1986 a survey of conditions of urban services in cities in the
north-east Chinese province of Liaoning was conducted under the joiut effort
of the Australian International Development Assistance Bureau (AIDAB), the
UNDP RAS 81/001 Project and the World Bank. The survey identified water
supply, wastewater management, water pollution control and urban transport as
major problem areas.  Further work was thien carried out by thie Liaoning
Government assisted by consultants financed under an A$4 million grant from
AIDAB to formulate strategic plans for water resource developrtient, water and
wastewater management, water pollution control and urban transport improvement
for cities in the basins of the Hun and Taizi Rivers which contain the
heaviest urban and industrial concentration in the province.5 Cities
involved in water, wastewater and water pollution control included: Shenyang
(city district population of 3.25 million), Fushun (1.08 million), Anshan
(1.09 million), Benxi (0.68 million), Liaoyang (0.43 million), and Yingkou
(0.36 million). Shenyang, Anshan and Fushun were also involved in urban
transport. The execution of this work was supervised by the Bank Group under
a memorandum of understanding with AIDAB. In addition the Liaoning Government
also concurrently conducted water supply and pollution control studies for
Fuxin (0.55 million) and Dandong (0.45 million), two additional important
provincial cities located in the Daling River and the Yalu River basins.
2.2       Through the above efforts, long term plans have been developed and
priority investments identified for the province estimated at about Y4.5
billion (in 1988 prices) or about US$1.0 billion (at the prevailing exchange
rate) for water supply, sewerage, and water pollution control works; and Yl.25
billion or US$0.27 billion for urban transport works, as well as important
institutional development work needed to strengthen these subsectors. Because
of the size of the plans, and the time needed by the province to plan and
absorb the investments required, the works will be implemented over a period
of about 15 years. This project, which constitutes the first investment
slice, consists of the most urgent works recommended in the plans and
important institutional measures for the improvement of water supply for the
cities of Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou and of urban transport in the city of
Shenyang, as well as initial efforts to address industrial water pollution
problems. The AIDAB consultants (para. 2.1) have also been instrumental in
conducting feasibility studies for the various project components. A second
project that would focus on water pollution abatement in the river basins has
also been proposed in accordance with the development plans. The planning and
design of the second project is already in hand, and technical assistance to
support it will be provided from this project.
The Project Area
2.3       The area under this project comprises the cities of Shenyang,
Yingkou and Fuxin in Liaoning Province. The province has a population of
5    The  Hun-Taizi  River  basins  cover  about  20  per  cent  of  the

population.   About 60 per cent of Liaoning's industrial output is
concentrated in six major cities in these basins, Six other cities
share another 20 per cent of this industrial output.

about 36 million, with 25 million classified as urban6, and has important
iron ore, coal and oil resources, enabling it to become China's majoI bhase for
industry7.  The province has also a significant agricultural output8.
Shenyang, the provincial capital, specializes in machine building. Yingkou,
which is an important seaport, has a mix of industries with heavier
concentration in machine building and textiles. Fuxin, a city in the nortlh-
west hilly region, is involved primarily with coal and power generation.
Annex 1 provides further background information on the three cities.
Existing Water Supply and Environment Situation
2.4       The studies mentioned in para. 2.1 have identified severe water
shortages in a number of Liaoning cities. The worst conditions are those
found in the cities of Shenyang, Yingkou and Fuxin, and these have been
selected for financing in the project. Within the built-up areas of the
cities, which are the service areas of the water supply companies, all
residential and institutional users are served. Most industrial users within
the service areas are also supplied, but some of these users have been
extracting directly untreated water for their own supplies, either from
groundwater or from nearby water courses.
2.5       Water demand in the three cities has already exceeded production
capacity, and supply restrictions have been imposed on both industrial and
domestic consumptions. It is estimated that without improvement, together
with measures to curb demand, production capacities in the cities will fall
short of demand by 60 percent to 120 percent in 1995 and 120 percent to 350
percent in the year 2000.
2.6       The piped water supply in the cities is acceptable for drinking
purposes from a bacteriological point of view after it has been treated and
disinfected. Disinfected water that is distributed can often become
contaminated, however, through ingress of dirty groundwater into the
distribution pipe system during periods of low, and often negative, water
pressure which occur when supply fails to meet demand. To alleviate the
situation the water companies try to maintain a relatively high chlorine
residual in the distributed water. Another water quality problem is the

residents of whom 2,000 or more are non-agricultural population
living in the site of the township government, or an area inhabited
by at least 20,000 residents of whom 10 percent or more are non-
agricultural population living in the site of the township
government.
Liaoning produces 7.2 percent of China's gross industrial output,
with a gross per capita output of Y3416 (1988) which is about 2.1
times the national average.   In terms of gross heavy industrial
output Liaoning produces 9.4 percent of the national output.

constitutes about 15 percent of the total provincial output.

of env'ironmental concern in the past, have caused serious water pollution
pilo)lems in many waterways of the province. The situation is most severe in
the Htutn and Taizi river basins, where a large part of surface flows have been
rendered unsafe for human consumption due to the uncontrolled discharge of
industrial effluents containing toxic matters and heavy metals. The Liaoning
Environmental Protection Bureau is already tightening enforcement of
regulations for reducing industrial water pollution, particularly on the
removal of toxic matters and heavy metals. An action program has been drawn
up for the various municipalities to work out with polluting industries a
timed plan for reducing pollution discharges,
2.9       In all cities, including the project cities, plans are being
developed for the construction of sewers and sewage treatment plants to
collect and appropriately dispose of municipal wastewater. These plans would
require very large investments. Studies are being carried out to identify
less expensive methods of sewage treatment which may help relieve some of the
capital and operating cost burdens. The water resource and water pollution
control studies carried out in the province (para. 2.1) have proposed a
program of works for wastewater treatment facilities that could produce the
best result for improving water quality of the river systems given the
financial constraints. On the basis of these studies, a project which focuses
on wastewater management and water pollution abatement in three major cities
of the Hun-Taizi River basins, to immediately follow the proposed project, has
been planned for Bank Group assistance. This project would also provide
support for industrial pollution reduction, including waste minimization
through process modification, recycling and conversion to the use of non-toxic
inputs, as well as effluent treatment.
Status of Existing Urban Transport
2.1O      Rapid economic expansion is placing heavy demands on the entire
transport system of the province. Motor vehicles in Liaoning cities now total
about 150,000. In addition there are about 3.5 million non-motor driven vehi-
cles, mainly bicycles, which are expected to remain as the chief mode of
passenger travel for many years. Recent statistics in Shenyang, where the
urban transport component of the project will be located, show that the number
of motor vehicles has tripled and that for bicycles have nearly doubled to
154,000 and 3.0 million respectively during the period 1982-1989. Bus rider-
ship, on the other hand, has leveled off, and recently declined, a phenomenon
which is partially explained by the deterioration in bus service caused by
lack of investment in equipment and rapidly increasing operating costs.
Bicycles dominate peak-period traffic flows in Shenyang, and account for 80



- 10 -
percent of all notn-walking trips, with buses accounting for another 1/
percent. Thie city is served by a fleet of about 1,200 buses and trolley-
buses, and another 2,000 buses are owned by enterprises and are used for
transporting employees to and from work.  Due to street congestion the buses
have a difficult time competing during peak hours with bicycles faster by
almost 50 percent in door-to-door journey times. Poor traffic managemenit
further exacerbates tihe situation. The present wide variety of vehiicle types
with their varying speeds is causing serious congestion, delays and accidents.
III. DEMAND FOR URBAN WATER AND TRANSPORT SERVICES
Population Growth
3.1       From 1977 to 1986, population in Liaoning cities9 grew at an
average rate of about 4 percent p.a.. The high growth rate was attributed
mainly to very active migration from rural areas of the province. Migration
rates reached a peak of 7.7 percent p.a. in 1978, and have been declining
since then, dropping to 0.8 percent in 1986. It is estimated that, while some
resurgence of rural to urban migration may occur, a resumption of the high
migration rates of the past is unlikely.  With decreasing birth rate, the net
population growth rate in Liaoning Uities is expected to approach the national
average population growth rate of about 0.8 percent p.a. in the year 2000.

3.3       Residential and Institutional Water Use.  Traditionally,
residential and institutional water use in Chinese cities are intimately
linked. Due to the lack of plumbing facilities in older homes, most of the
domestic ablution activities have been carried out at the work places of
workers. This has accounted for unusually low residential water use in the
past, with correspondingly high institutional water use. More recent figures
show that while institutional use is still increasing, its ratio to domestic
use is declining in Shenyang, showing a gradual shift to household water use
in new homes with better plumbing facilities. As restrictions to the present
heavy demands are relieved with water made available through the proposed
project, and with rapidly rising incomes, unrestricted residential and



- 12 -
institutionial per capita water conisumption in the three citites is expected to
grow at a relatively high ratu of 3.0 percent p.a..  However, witth a gen(eral
scarcity of water resourctes in the regiotn, the cities would still find it
necessary to impose hoth phvsical and pricing measures for demand inanagement
in order to avoid heavy future investmenits, and more modest growthi levels are
therefore expected.  Aninex 2 provides projected residential alid institutional
per capita anid daily water demands for the period 1989 to 2000 --or situations,
of both normal and strict water conservation enforcement (using price and
quota measures).
3.4       Industrial Water Use.  About 60 percent of the total municipal
water supply in the three cities are used by industries.  Industrial water
consumption is expected to grow further given the 8.7 percent p.a. industrial
growth projected by the Government for the next 10 years.  A survey conducted
by the cities on water use by various types of industries, with water
consumption per Y10,000 of industrial output used as a criterion, showed water
use to be two to five times higher than similar industries in many developed
countries. In an effort to conserve water, the cities are requiring most
existing industries to improve water consumption efficiency, through imposing
a penalty for water consumption beyond the quota set for each major industry.
New industries are allocated water amounts based on established and reasonable
industry norms which reflect prudent water use.
3.5       In projecting industrial water demands for Shenyang, apart from the
assumption of an industrial output growth of 8.7 percent p.a., we have assumed
improved water use efficiency, resulting in a reduction of unit water use to
65 percent of the 1989 levels by year 2000 with normal conservation measures,
and to 50 percent of 1989 levels under strict water conservation enforcement.
The overall results give a net industrial water demand growth rate of 4.7
percent and 2.7 percent p.a. respectively for the two cases.  For Yingkou and
Fuxin, most of the industrial water demand growth is attributed to new
industries. Annex 2 shows the projected industrial demands.
3.6       Unaccounted for water was reported to be less than 10 percent in
each of the three cities, but this figure cannot be substantiated. There is
very little leakage control, and leaks are repaired when they become visible
at the ground surface or begin to affect water pressure. With the presence of
old pipes in many areas of the cities, the ability to maintain unaccounted for
water at this low level is debatable. The situation will worsen as water
pressures are raised when the water supply is improved as a result of the
proposed project. A more realistic value of the unaccounted for water of 15
percent has been used for the purpose of estimating total water demands,
assuming that measures to control leakage proposed in this project (para.
5.13) would be implemented,
3.7       As th  urban water supply system shares with other users the same
water resources in the region, to achieve the goal of optimizing water
resource use, a concerted effort by all users to conserve water will,
therefore, be necessary. For this purpose, assurances were obtained from the
Liaoning Government during negotiations to: (a) carry out, with the assistance
of experienced consultants and based on terms of reference and timing
satisfactory to the Association, a study on the pricing of water resources for
agriculture and urban water supply in the Hun-Taizi River Basin region, as
well as other measures for water conservation; and (b) discuss the results of
the study with the Association, and implement its recommendations after they
have been agreed. Draft terms of reference for the study, given in Annex 3,
were also discussed and geeneral agreemernt reached.

based on a systematic review of Shenyang's existing and future transport
problems and demands, and conforms with the city's long term master plan f or-
urban development. An immediate need of Shenyang is the relief of severe
traffic congestion in the city. Diagnostic studies carried out by the
consultants have measured this in terms of volumes for vehicles and bicycles,
accident rates, and width of road corridors (see Annex 4). During the period
1982 to 1988, the number of motorized vehicles grew at an average rate of 16.5
percent p.a., while bicycles, which are considerably larger in number, grew at
a rate of 6 percent p.a. (see Annex 5). Future rates of increase are expected
to slow to 7 percent and 3 percent p.a. respectively. The main problem to be
corrected is the uncontrolled use of road space by motorized vehicles,
bicycles, and pedestrian. In order that major investments for road
construction can be deferred, much work has to be done to streamline traffic
flow and to improve travellers' use of public transport.  To achieve this,
road congestion will have to be reduced to allow public transport travel times
to be decreased, and bus routings would have to be rationalized.  Stricter
enforcement of road discipline and better road signs and markings would be
required to improve road safety.
3.10       Public transport vehicles of the city have average ages of 12-14
years, and some of the overhaul repair facilities are 40-50 years old.  Some
of the vehicles are in dire need of major overhauls and many should be
retired.  However to reduce the requirzment for large capital investment in
new vehicles, the transport companies have embarked on depot modernization
programs for vehicle overhaul that will both reduce the time in-the-shop and
increase overhaul capacity. New structures have either been completed or will
be completed by the end of 1990 to house the new vehicle overhaul operations.
Road Maintenance Needs
3.11       At present only those roads that come under the Road M'1aintenance
Division of the Urban Construction Bureau are being adequately maintained.
These comprise about one-half of the total road network (joout 2,562 km.),
mainly comprising the first and second class roads. T;his condition is largely
due to lack of proper maintenance equipment anLd tlb: absence of a strategy that
includes preventive maintenance and less expensive maintenance techniques.
IV. THE PROPOSED PROJECT
Proiect Obiectives
4.1        The project is part the first slice of a de-elopment program which
has broad objectives of improving the utilization and management of water
resources and the management of urban transport, two of the most critical
areas of concern in the development of Liaoning province. Specific objectives



- 14 -
ut thte project are: (a) to improve water supply conditions in the cities of
Shenyarig, Yitngkou and Fuxin through physical works, and strengthening of
institutions, regulations, management, financial and pricing policies in the
,AihLsctor; (b) to improve traffic and public transport conditions in Shenyang
through1 a pilot program of selected low-cost physical works as well as
strengthening of institutions responsible for planning, managing and operating
transport systems, and of traffic regulations and their enforcement; and (c)
to inprove measures for water pollution abatement through technical assistance
to fintd effective treatment processes, strengthen institutions and enforcement
measures for water pollution control, and develop the human resources required
to implement this program.
Rationale for IDA Involvement
4.2       Liaoniirg is an important industrial base, and a province which is
experiencing one of the highest urban growth rates in China, with
corresponding pressures for urban service and environmental needs. The
province is also one of the most enterprising in the country, and has been
actively pursuing economic reforms. Faced with the pressing need to improve
efficiency of urban services and quality of the environment, the province has
turned to the Association for assistance, particularly in the areas of
institutional development and management of urban and environmental services.
The project will assist the Liaoning Provincial Government and the municipal
governments to build upon earlier donor-supported planning and programming
efforts. It will set appropriate sector policies and regulations with regard
to water resource management, water supply, water pollution control and urban
transport, and will strengthen institutions in these sectors in operations
aimed at achieving cost recovery, efficient use of water and road space, and
effective water pollution control. Liaoning Province having recently embarked
on a major investment program for urban and environmental services,
Association assistance is particularly useful at this stage in helping to
create the institutional framework needed for long term development of the
sectors, to provide advice on major investment decisions, and to support the
continuation of the development program in the planning of the next slice of
the investment program focussed on water polluttion abatement. The Central
Government strongly supports the project, and aims to have the measures intro-
duced in this project to serve as a model for replication in other provinces
in China.
Project Description
4.3       The project would provide physical works and technical assistance
for institutional development in water supply for the provincial cities of
Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou, and iin urban transport for the city of Shenyang.
The physical works of the water supply component would include the construc-
tion of transmission pipelines from existing storage reservoirs, pumping
stations, treatment works, supply and distribution pipes, and improvements to
the existing water supply networks for the water supply companies of the three
cities. The institutional aspect for the water supply component would streng-
then the water companies, as well as the Liaoning Water Resource Commission
in: (a) developing and enforcing adequate water regulations; (b) establishing
appropriate water resource and water supply pricing policies; (c) improving
water operation practices; (d) promoting measures for water conservation; and
(e) training of staff. On water pollution control, the project would provide
technical assistance to the Environmental Protection Bureaus of Liaoning
Province and of the three municipalities to (a) study methods for pollution
source treatment; (b) study available types of equipment for treatment and



- 15 -
regulations; (d) purchase equipment and instruments for water pollution
monitoring, and a mobile laboratory and equipment for water quality monitoring
work; and (e) train staff engaged in water pollution control work. The
project would also provide technical assistance to the Liaoning Construction
Commission and the Liaoning Environmental Protection Bureau to plan a second
phase project which would focus largely on sewerage and wastewater treatment
work required for water pollution control.
4.4       The urban transport component would assist the Shenyang Urban
Construction Bureau to carry out traffic corridor improvements, and procure
equipment for maintenance of roads. Workshop equipment for maintenance and
repair will also be procured for the Shenyang Bus and Trolley-bus Companies.
Included also would be technical assistance to the Shenyang Construction
Commission and the Traffic Brigades of the Shenyang Public Security Bureau
for: (a) formulating better urban transport management policies; (b) planning
projects; (c) introducing advanced traffic system management techniques and
safety enforcement; (d) strengthening of operation and maintenance of the bus
and trolley-bus companies; and (e) staff training.
4.5       Details of the various project components are given in Annex 6.  A
summary of these components is given below:
(a) Shenyana Water Suppllv: (US$52.7 million). Construction of about 51
km. of water transmission pipeline (single 2,200 mm dia. or twin
1,600 mm dia., 400,000 m3), and 32 km. of distribution pipelines
(500 mm to 1,200 mm dia.).
(b) Fuxin Water Supply: (US$27.0 million). Construction of intake
works, sedimentation basin and pumping station at Naodehai
Reservoir, about 74 km. of water transmission pipeline (900 mm to
1,600 mm dia., 100,000 m3 per day), 2 booster pump stations, water
treatment plant, and about 14 km. of supply pipeline (900 mm to
1,200 mm dia.) to the city network.
(c) Yingkou Water Supplv: (US$18.4 million). Construction of about 57
km. of water transmission pipeline (500 to 900 mm dia.), water
intake at Daliao River (120,000 mi3 per day), pumping station, about
49 km. of distribution pipelines (300 mm to 900 mm dia.), and
improvements to existing water treatment plants.
(d) Water Pollution Control: (US$1.8 million). Procurement of
equipment and instruments for environmental pollution monitoring,
and a mobile laboratory and equipment for water quality monitoring
work.
(e)  Shenyang Urban Transport: (US$20.8 million).  Improvement of about
44 km. of arterial road corridors; procurement of maintenance and
repair equipment for bus and trolley-bus depots and garages;
improvement of operation management for bus routing and scheduling,
maintenance and financial control; procurement of road maintenance
and road safety (line marking and signing) equipment, and
implementation of a computerized road maintenance system.
(f) Proiect SupRort Technical Assistance (Engineering-related) (US$3.1
million), for: (i) advising on project management and construction
supervision; and (ii) consultants for the preparation of a second
phase project.

(g) Capacity Building Technical Assistance (Institution-related)
(US$1.6 million), for: (i) experts to provide techntical anid
financial advice to the management of the water supply companies:
(ii) technical experts to provide advice to the management of
public transport companies in Shenyang; (iii) technical experts to
advise on urban transport management and road saferv enforcement;

water supply companies, and other staff engaged in water supply,

(h) Policy Development Technical Assistance (Institution-related)
(US$0.8 million), for: (i) studies on water resource and water
supply pricing; and effective methods for industrial wastewater
treatment, including the strengthening of environmental protection
laws and regulations.
Proiect Cost Estimates
4.6       Project cost estimates are based on engineering designs prepared bN
Liaoning provincial and municipal officials with the assistance of local
consultants and consultants financed by AIDAB. The unit prices used come fro;r
several sources: (a) quotations on equipment and materials from foreign and
local suppliers; (b) construction costs according to prices published by the
Government, adjusted for inflation; (c) prices for goods and works from recent
contracts in China; and (d) composite unit construction costs for system
components used in forelgn countries for estimating purposes. Goods imported
for the project with credit proceeds are exempt from import duties and taxes.
A physical contingency of 10 percent of the base cost has been added. Local
price contingencies assume price increases of 10 percent in 1991, 8 percent ill
1992, and 5 percent p.a. thereafter: foreign price contingencies used are 9
percent in 1991, 1.1 percent in 1992, and 2.95 percent p.a. thereafter.
4.7       The total estimated project cost is US$126.2 million (Y700
million), with a foreign exchange component of US$75.2 million (60 percent).
The total financing required, which includes US$2.4 million of interest during
construction is US$128.6 million (Y712 million). A detailed breakdown of the
estimated cost of the proposed project is in Annex 7 and is summarized in
Table 4.1.

4.9       The IDA credit would be made to the People's Republic of China
(GOC). The credit would be for a 35-year term including a 10-year grace
period. The proceeds of the IDA credit would be onlent to Liaoning Province
(LPG) on terms and conditions satisfactory to the As'jociation, which are



- 18 -
expected to be at a fixed interest of 5.5 percent p.a. for a 15-year period
including five years grace. LPG would onlend the proceeds to the Shenyang
Municipal Government (SMG), Fuxin Municipal Government (FMG) and Yingkou
Municipal Government (YMG).  Three onlending agreements, one each for SMG, FMG
and YMG, will be concluded between LPG and the municipal governments.
OnMlending terms would be at a fixed interest rate of 5.5 percent for a 15-year
period including five years grace. SMG, FMC and YMG will bear all foreign
exchange risks.
4.10      LPC would also cause the proceeds to be used for water supply
construction to be further onlent to the Shenyang Water Supply Company (SWSC),
the Fuxin Water Supply Company (FWSC) and the Yingkou Water Supply Company
(YWSC) at the variable interest rate payable on medium/long-term Renminbi
loans by the People's Construction Bank of China (PCBC) for a 15 year period
including five years of grace. This rate is currently around 8 to 10 percent
p.a..
4.11      Since the urban transport components of the project are for low-
cost enhancements with the objective of improving the operating efficiency of
the existing investments, the project funds will be passed on to the agencies
included in the public transport component as grants.
4.12      Agreement was reached on the onlending terms and conditions with
the GOC and LPG at negotiations. In addition, the subsidiary loan agreements
between the Municipalities and the Water Supply Companies which define
onlending terms acceptable to the Association, obligations for project
execution and the financial and institutional objectives to be set for the
water supply companies of the three municipalities were discussed at
negotiations. Approval of the Development Credit Agreement by the State
Council and execution of these subsidiary loan agreements, satisfactory to
Association, would be conditions of credit effectiveness.
Status of Engineering
4.13      The project was prepared by Chinese project teams established in
each of the three municipalities for the water supply and the urban transport
components, with assistance from major local design institutes"1, and
consultants funded by AIDAB. The teams were coordinated by a provincial
project office under the Liaoning Construction Commission (LCC). Feasibility
studies for the various components of the project have been reviewed by the
Association. Local and foreign consultants have been engaged to carry out
final detailed design and preparation of tender documents, which have now been
completed.
The North-east Municipal Engineering Design Institute of Changchun
for the Shenyang water component; the Beijing Municipal Engineering
Design Institute for the Yingkou water component; the Liaoning
Province Water and Electric Power Investigation Design Institute,
and the Liaoning Province Urban Planning Design and Research
Institute for the Fuxin water component; and the Shenyang Municipal
Engineering, Design and Research Institute for the Shenyang urban
transport component.



- 19 -
Consultant Services
4.14      Foreign consultants were engaged using funds from the Technical
Cooperation Credit (TCC) and UNDP (Umbrella Project) to carry out with local
consultants and counterpart staff the detailed design and preparation of bid
documents, Included in the project cost estimates are tlIQ services of
consultants required to: (a) advise on project management and construction
supervision; (b) carry out project-related studies on water supply, urban
transport and environmental protection; (c) provide technical and financial
advice to the water supply and public transport companies; and (d) prepare a
second phase project.   The total consultant (foreign and local) and
counterpart staff requirements for the project are shown in Annex 8.
4.15      Consultant services for about 270 staff-months are estimated at a
total cost of US$4.9 million, including salary, costs, fees, international
travel and subsistence. The Liaoning and the municipal governments would
provide about 1,800 staff-months of local consultants and counterpart staff
for the work. During negotiations assurances were obtained from the Liaoning
Government that it would engage consultants satisfactory to the Association to
advise on project management and supervision of project construction,
conducting of project-related studies, and providing managerial, technical and
financial advice to the water supply companies, public transport companies,
and the road maintenance department.
Staff Training and Development
4.16      Training programs have been proposed by the provincial and
municipal project offices. For project staff this would include training
seminars on project management, contract management and construction
supervision. Training courses would also be held for water supply, urban
transport and environmental protection staff on water supply and wastewater
management, environmental protection control, bus transport management, road
maintenance management, and computer applications. The project would also
provide technical assistance and training equipment to improve the existing
training centers for operators in the water supply and relevant urban
transport organizations. Quality control inspectors will be trained in local
vocational institutions. Training in local institutions of higher learning
would also be provided to middle managers and financial and accounting staff
of the water companies and trainers of water operators, some of whom will be
selected for training abroad. Visits by senior managers of the water
companies to study water supply management practices in foreign countries
would also be financed. Detailed training proposals, together with an
estimate of the number and type of staff to be trained, and cost estimates are
presented in Annex 15. During negotiations assurances were obtained from the
Liaoning Government that it would cause the training program to be implemented
in accordance with the agreed plan and timing as stated in the Annex.
4.17      The project will provide 36 staff-months of technical and financial
management expert time to assist the three water supply companies in
strengthening their operations. The advisors would be assigned to work
closely with local staff in the water supply companies. Draft terms of
reference for the advisors are in Annex 19.
4.18      Although the Shenyang Bureau of Urban Construction and the
associated operating institutions and design institutes have a large number of
well-trained engineers in urban transport, they lack state-of-the-art
knowledge in design and p'lanning. They also do not have previous experience



- 20 -
in the Bank/Association's procurement procedures. On-the-job training has
been provided by the foreign consultants that assisted in project
identification, feasibility studies and the preliminary design. A technrical
assistance program will train core staff in urban transport in fundamentals of
traffic engineering, public transport workshop operations, road maintenance
operations and traffic/road safety enforcement.
Project Management
4.19      A provincial project office under LCC, the Liaoning Urban
Construction and Renewal Project Office (LUCRPO), has been set up with a
mandate from the Liaoning Provincial Government. Four municipal level project
offices, one each for the water component in the three cities, and one for
urban transport in Shenyang, have also been established to carry out project
preparation and execution. The project offices have been staffed, with plans
for staff additions to match project implementation needs. The project
management organization is shown in Annex 9. During negotiations assurances
were obtained from the Liaoning Government that it would cause the project
municipalities to maintain the project offices established to facilitate
implementation, with functions and responsibilities satisfactory to the
Association, and with competent staff in adequate numbers.
4.20      Improvements in the traffic conditions brought about by the
corridor improvements cannot be projected precisely. For this purpose
measurements of traffic conditions (travel speed, waiting time at
intersections, traffic accidents, etc.) would be taken by project staff before
and after the improvements have been constructed. Consultants have included
plans for this work in the overall design. During implementation of the
project, should the improvements in traffic conditions not meet expectations,
corrective actions, which may include revisions in traffic engineering plans
and stricter enforcement of traffic discipline, will be taken.
Procurement
4.21      Procurement procedures and arrangements satisfactory to the
Association have been agreed with Liaoning Province. All procurement
activities will be organized through the Shenyang Machinery and Electric
Equipment Tendering Corporation (SYMEETC), an experienced procurement agency
in China which has been contracted by LUCRPO to carry out the work.
International competitive bidding (ICB) will be carried out under the auspices
of the China Machinery Corporation (CMC), which is one of several procurement
agencies in China involved in international procurement work on World Bank
projects.
4.22      Of the civil works and goods procurement packages, about 14 will be
awarded through ICB, seven through local competitive bidding (LCB), and the
remaining will be processed through other methods. Civil works have been
grouped together to the maximum extent possible to enable more of the works to
be awarded through ICB. All civil works contracts costing more than US$3.0
million and equipment contracts costing more than US$200,000 will be subject
to the Association's prior review. Annex 10 lists the contract packages with
the method of procurement and Table 4.3 summarizes the procurement categories
with the expected procurement methods.

4.23      Civil Works.  Contracts with an estimated value of US$37.5 million,
consisting of seven water supply contracts will be awarded to prequalified
contractors under ICB procedures consistent with the Association's Guidelines.
Qualifying domestic contractors will receive a preference in bid evaluation of
7.5 percent. Contracts amounting to US$14.5 million for water supply
structures and US$8.1 million for corridor improvement will be contracted
through LCB procedures that are acceptable to the Association. Interested
foreign bidders would be allowed to bid on these LCB contracts. One project
component costing about US$2.1 million, to construct a pipeline across the Hun
River, has been carried out using force account under advanced procurement
arrangements. This method of procurement was deemed necessary in view of the
urgency of the work and the need to accomplish the work during the very short
period when the river was at low flow.
4.24      Eguipment and Materials.  The packages for equipment and materials
for the water supply component would include one package with several
subcomponents for pipe materials and contracts for equipment supply. Packages
for urban transport equipment would include public transport workshop
equipment, road maintenance equipment, and traffic signals. These equipment
and materials contracts, totaling US$51.4 million, will be procured under ICB
procedures. Qualifying domestic suppliers will receive a preference in bid
evaluation of 15 percent or custom duties and import taxes whichever is less.
In addition, small meters, instruments and other miscellaneous equipment



- 22 -
totaling about US$0.6 million will be procured through other procurement
procedures (Local Shopping) acceptable to the Association.
4.25      Technical Assistance.  Consultants retained under the project will
be recruited according to the "Guidelines on the Use of Consultants by the
World Bank and its Borrowers". Local consultants and counterpart staff will
be engaged by or assigned from the local government departments to work along
with foreign consultants on detailed design (work already completed),
preparation of bid documents (work already completed), project management and
construction supervision, conducting of project-related studies, and
preparation of a phase two project. Consulting firms will be invited to
submit proposals for the construction supervision work, the conducting of
project related studies and for the preparation of a phase two project.
4.26      Advanced Procurement.  In view of the relatively short construction
season (about six months) in Liaoning Province and the urgency of some works,
advanced contracting would be needed. To hasten project execution, 13
contracts estimated to cost about US$60 million would be awarded before credit
signing. These works are: (a) headworks construction for the Fuxin water
supply; (b) road corridor improvements (4 roads); (c) 6 contracts for pipe
materials for Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou; (d) 4 contracts for civil works for
construction of water supply pipeline (about 51 kilometers) for the Shenyang
water supply; and (e) pipeline across the Hun River (work already completed).
All contracts will be procured ir accordance with the Association's
Procurement Guidelines, and the normal review process by the Association will
be followed.

4.28      A Special Account with an authorized allocation of US$5.2 million,
based on four months' average disbursements, would be established.
Replenishment would be made on a monthly basis or whenever the Special Account
is drawn down to 50 percent of its initial deposit value. Disbursements for
training, civil works carried out by force account, cont;acts of civil works,
goods and services valued at less than US$200,000 would be made on the basis
of statements of expenditures (SOEs) to be certified by LUCRPO. Documents
supporting the SOEs would be retained by the LUCRPO and made available for
inspection by Association supervision missions. All other disbursements will
be made against fully documented expenditures.
4.29      The disbursement schedule (Annex 11) assumes a period of five
years, instead of 5.5 years in the standard disbursement schedule for China.



- 23 -
Project preparation and detailed design have been completed and procurement is
proceeding expeditiously. In additon the construction works are relatively
straight forward. There is also a keen interest on the part of the
beneficiary to implement the urgently required works. The shorter
disbursement period is therefore considered to be reasonable. Project
completion is estimated to be June 30, 1995, and the IDA credit closing date
would be June 30, 1996.  Retroactive financing of up to US$7   million for
expenditures after December 1, 1989 covering the 13 contracts listed in para.
4.26 will be provided.
Land Acquisition and Resettlement
4.30      Comprehensive surveys carried out by the three municipalities have
identified the land to be acquired for pump stations, treatment plant,
pipelaying, and street improvement. Where the works are to be constructed on
agricultural land and would be buried after construction, the land would be
rented during construction and returned to the farmers for use after work
completion. A relatively small number of houses have to be demolished and the
number of people to be resettled is about 360 (90 families). All persons are
expected to be resettled in the same neighborhood. Liaoning has land
acquisition regulations which outline the procedures and compensations
required. These compensations, amounting to US$5.9 million, have been
included in the project cost estimates.
4.31      The municipalities anticipate no difficulty in carrying out land
acquisition and resettlement (in fact some of the land required for the
project has already been acquired). Each city has a team responsible for land
acquisition and resettlement, and preparation work in this area is now well
advanced. The resettlement plan and the schedule prepared by the cities
(Annex 12) are satisfactory to the Association. During negotiations
assurances were obtained from the Liaoning Government that it would carry out
resettlement of persons affected by the project in a manner and according to a
schedule which is satisfactory to the Association. An understanding on the
various steps to be taken for resettlement was reached and recorded in the
minutes of negotiations.
Monitoring Criteria
4.32      The proposed project implementation schedule is shown in Annex 13.
Financial monitoring indicators for the water supply companies are in Annex
24. Reports on project implementation progress and on the operations of the
water supply companies would be prepared by LUCRPO and sent to the Association
quarterly commencing July 1, 1991. A project completion report reviewing the
planned objectives and the achievements of the project, including costs and
benefits derived, and performance and contribution of all parties associated
with project execution and system operation would be prepared by LUCRPO and
submitted to the Association within six months following the closing date of
the IDA credit.
V. THE BENEFICIARIES
Provincial and Municipal Institutions
5.1       The Liaoning Provincial Government is headed by a governor assisted
by five vice-governors, each of whom oversees several commissions and/or
departments. Various provincial commissions, departments and bureaus provide

5.2       With few exceptions, the organizations of the municipal governments
of Shenyang, Fuxin and Yingkou are essentially similar. Municipal affairs are
overseen by the Municipal Economic and Planning Commission (Yingkou and Fuxin
have separate economic conimissions and planning commissions), and the
Municipal Urban and Rurial Construction Commission (MURCC). The MURCC
supervises a number of bUreaus which are responsible for the physical
planning, design, construction, operation and maintenance of the urban
infrastructure, and  iot envirornmental protection.  In addition several bureaus
concerned with urban intrastructure report directly to the office of the
mayor. These include the Finance Bureau, the Water Conservancy Bureau, the
Bureau of Public Health and thie Public Security Bureau.  Organization charts
of the Liaoning Provincial Covernment and the municipal governments of the
three project cities are in Annex 16.
The Water Supply Compn1alies
5.3       Each of tlhe project cities has a water supply company, the Shenyang
Water Supply Company (SWSC). the Fuxin Water Supply Company (FWSC) and the
Yingkou Water Supply Company (YWSC), with a charter that allows it a degree of
financial autonomy (paras. 5.4 and 6.1 to 6.4). Regulation of the water
supply companies rests witlh a citY bureau (the Urban and Rural Construction
Commission in Shenvang, and the Urban Construction Bureaus in Fuxin and
Yingkou).  Organization charts of the water companies are shown in Annex 17.
The companies are mainly responsible for the provision of piped water to
residential, institutional and industrial consumers within their authorized
service areas, which normallv cover the entire built-up areas of the cities.
5.4       In recent Years, the companies have been allowed more financial
autonomy than in the past. Managers are given the freedom to explore better
ways to achieve opera:ioni efficiency in order to make higher profits, a
designated portion of wlhicht is shared among workers. Company departments
which were formerl en1gageed in meter manufacturing and maintenance, pipe
manufacture and pipeline construction exclusively for the company have been
restructured as subsidiary companies of the parent water company with self-
accounting and profit-making objectives, and are encouraged to seek business
outside the parent company. The companies are empowered to: (a) borrow funds
for working capital and investment, and issue short-term bonds with the
approval of the municipal government; (b) protect water sources and prosecute
polluters; (c) cut off water supply to consumers who fail to pay their bills;
and (d) impose appropriate plumbing standards. While the water supply
companies can earn profits, the amount of profit they can retain is limited
(para. 6.2).
5.5       All water tariff increases have to be justified and approved at the
municipal governr-fr-t '''f ;  Tllf responsible agency for processing requests



2 5 -
for tar-iff increases is thle municipal construction commission.  Where a
ju.titiable water tariff is not approved for political or social reasons, the
w:terr companies are compensated by the governments for any resulting losses.
